10495

10496<section class="blog-post">

10497

10498 <p>

10499Titration, is the process of slowly increasing one medicine or one liquid, with another medicine, liquid or pretty much anything.</p>

10500<p>

10501When relating to Cannabinoids, as dosable cannabis medicines are rapidly becoming available, it is becoming more and more important clinically to be able to titrate the cannabinoids. We all have so much to learn in this area, but these are my initial thoughts. I openly encourage comments.</p>

10502<p>

105031. For the majority of patients with simple anxiety/insomnia, it is very simple and rarely is any titration necessary. Generally 4 mg or 4 sprays/day is adquate.</p>

10504<p>

105052. For the seriously ill or seriously in pain, &nbsp;just using pure whole plant CBD is inadequate; patients require THC. Now comes the titrating. I generally suggest the patient build up a base of CBD, with very little THC. Perhaps somewhere between 10 and 20 mg, we begin adding THC 2 mg (one spray), increased every other day. This seems to minimize the psychoactivity.</p>

10506<p>

10507It is very clear clinically, at least in my experience, that adding THC to a baseline CBD regimen is a good way to initiate many patients programs. The baseline of CBD seems to greatly help the THC side effects.</p>

10508

10509 <div class="blog-author">

10510

10511 <span class="author-tag">

10512Author</span>

10513

10514 <div class="author-img-container">

10515

10516 <img src="https://sa1s3optim.patientpop.com/assets/images/provider/photos/2033121.jpg" alt="">

10517

10518 <span class="author-name">

10519Allan Frankel, MD</span>

10520

10521 <span class="author-description">

10522Dr Allan Frankel is one of the few physicians in the US who truly understands Cannabis as a medicine. All treatments suggested have been well studied. Every patient seen by Dr Frankel is given a personally created Treatment Plan created with the patient&#039;s specific issues defined.

10523

10524Plant medicine requires &quot;tuning&quot; of the dosing. Dr Frankel works with his patients thru a messaging portal. The use of this portal, allows quick and simple follow up contact with Dr Frankel. Patients are not charged for these messages, as this is how Dr Frankel has learned what he has learned. Follow up appointments in person or by phone/video are also available when needed</span>

10933 var start = null, end = null, duration = 400, callback = function(){};

10934 for(var i=0; i<arguments.length; i++){

10935 if(typeof(arguments[i]) == 'string'){

10936 if(!start) start = arguments[i];

10937 else end = arguments[i];

10938 } else if(typeof(arguments[i]) == 'number'){

10939 duration = arguments[i];

10940 } else if(typeof(arguments[i]) == 'function'){

10941 callback = arguments[i];

10942 }

10943 }

10944 if(start && !end){

10945 end = start;

10946 start = null;

10947 }

10948 if(!end) return;

10949 if(start){

10950 this.css("transform", start);

10951 }

10952 if(duration < 16) duration = 16;

10953 var transitionB4 = this.css('transition');

10954 this.css('transition', 'transform ' + duration + 'ms');

10955 this.css('transform', end);

10956 var $el = this;

10957 setTimeout(function(){

10958 $el.css('transition', transitionB4 || '');

10959 $el.css('transform', end);

10960 callback();

10961 }, duration);

10962 };

10965(function($){

10966 $.fn.swipeHandler = function(options) {

10967 var $container = this;

10968 var swipeThreshold = options.swipeThreshold || null;

10969 var onSwipeLeft = options.onSwipeLeft || null;

10970 var onSwipeRight = options.onSwipeRight || null;

10971 $container.on('touchstart', function(event) {

10972 var previousSwipeX = event.originalEvent.touches[0].clientX;

10973 $container.on('touchend', removeSwipeListeners);

10974 $container.on('touchcancel', removeSwipeListeners);

10975 $container.on('touchmove', function(event) {

10976 currentSwipeX = event.originalEvent.touches[0].clientX;

10977 if(currentSwipeX-swipeThreshold >

10978 previousSwipeX){

10979 removeSwipeListeners();

10980 if ( onSwipeRight ){

10981 event.preventDefault();

10982 onSwipeRight(event);

10983 }

10984 }else if(currentSwipeX+swipeThreshold < previousSwipeX){

10985 removeSwipeListeners();

10986 if ( onSwipeLeft ){

10987 event.preventDefault();

10988 onSwipeLeft(event);

10989 }

10990 }

10991 previousSwipeX = currentSwipeX;

10992 });

10993 });

10994 function removeSwipeListeners() {

10995 $container.off('touchmove');

10996 $container.off('touchend');

10997 $container.off('touchcancel');

10998 }

10999 };

11000})(jQuery);

11004(function($,sr){

11005 // debouncing function from John Hann

11006 // http://unscriptable.com/index.php/2009/03/20/debouncing-javascript-methods/

11007 var debounce = function (func, threshold, execAsap) {

11008 var timeout;

11009 return function debounced () {

11010 var obj = this, args = arguments;

11011 function delayed () {

11012 if (!execAsap)

11013 func.apply(obj, args);

11014 timeout = null;

11015 };

11016 if (timeout)

11017 clearTimeout(timeout);

11018 else if (execAsap)

11019 func.apply(obj, args);

11020 timeout = setTimeout(delayed, threshold || 100);

11021 };

11022 }
